    1 | ================================================================================
    2 | ERIC'S COMPLETE WORKOUT LOG
    3 | Compiled: March 17, 2026
    4 | ================================================================================
    5 | 
    6 | 
    7 | EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
    8 | ================================================================================
    9 | 
   10 | Eric began his current structured weight training program in January 2023
   11 | at age 55, starting at 196 lbs. Over the following three-plus years through
   12 | March 2026 (age 58), he has completed 391 recorded training sessions totaling
   13 | over 8.1 million pounds of volume across weight lifting, martial arts, yoga,
   14 | and cardio activities.
   15 | 
   16 | TRAINING BACKGROUND
   17 | 
   18 | Eric has over 40 years of physical training history:
   19 |   - Tae Kwon Do, ages 12-18
   20 |   - Baguazhang, ages 28-29
   21 |   - Bagua Qigong, ages 31-51
   22 |   - Weight lifting in his 40s (prior to the current program)
   23 |   - Current program: January 2023 to present (age 55-58)
   24 | 
   25 | This martial arts foundation provided decades of body awareness, flexibility,
   26 | and functional movement before the current weight training program. The
   27 | January 2023 start was a return to structured lifting, not a beginning
   28 | from zero.
   29 | 
   30 | PROGRAM HISTORY
   31 | 
   32 | Eric followed three Jim Stoppani programs, progressing through each at his
   33 | own pace rather than the prescribed timeframes:
   34 | 
   35 |   1. Shortcut to Size (started Jan 2023) — A 12-week periodized program
   36 |      cycling through microcycles of decreasing reps and increasing weight
   37 |      across three phases. This built the foundation of his lifting technique
   38 |      and established his baseline strength.
   39 | 
   40 |   2. Beginner to Advanced (mid-2023) — A 12-week program progressing from
   41 |      whole-body training 3x/week to a 4-day split, introducing more
   42 |      exercises and training volume over time.
   43 | 
   44 |   3. HIIT 100 (started Jan 17, 2024) — A 6-week high-intensity program
   45 |      combining German Volume Training (10 sets of 10 reps) with
   46 |      progressively shorter rest periods, finishing each workout with
   47 |      100-rep sets and full-body finishers like dead-curl-presses.
   48 | 
   49 | After completing HIIT 100, Eric transitioned to a self-directed
   50 | combination regimen, blending elements from all three Stoppani programs
   51 | into a distinctive hybrid approach.
   52 | 
   53 | TRAINING PHILOSOPHY & FORM CORRECTIONS
   54 | 
   55 | Eric's current approach prioritizes effectiveness, injury prevention, and
   56 | longevity over ego lifting. Several deliberate form corrections have been
   57 | made since the program began:
   58 | 
   59 |   1. Squat depth — Corrected from half squats to full squats. Current
   60 |      working weights (135-165 lbs) at full depth represent more effective
   61 |      work than the earlier 225 lb half squats. This correction also
   62 |      resolved chronic knee pain.
   63 | 
   64 |   2. Bench press range — Corrected to full chest-touch on every rep.
   65 |      The current 175 lb max represents genuine full-range strength.
   66 | 
   67 |   3. Eliminating momentum — Stopped using body swing on curls and other
   68 |      lifts. All reps are now strict form with the muscles doing 100%
   69 |      of the work.
   70 | 
   71 |   4. Pec fly technique — Now starts from a rear delt fly position,
   72 |      achieving full stretch through the rear delts before engaging
   73 |      the chest for greater total muscle activation per rep.
   74 | 
   75 |   5. Machine seat height variation — Systematically changes seat height
   76 |      on machine exercises to work muscles from different angles.
   77 | 
   78 | HIGH-REP APPROACH
   79 | 
   80 | The current high-rep, moderate-weight methodology (100-rep sets with under
   81 | 30 seconds rest, all rest periods capped at 90 seconds in 2025) serves
   82 | multiple purposes simultaneously:
   83 | 
   84 |   - Cardiovascular conditioning — Elevated heart rate throughout sessions
   85 |     effectively combines cardio and resistance training, contributing to
   86 |     a sustained Superior VO2max rating.
   87 |   - Injury prevention — Lighter weights eliminate the wrist pain, shoulder
   88 |     pain, and joint stress experienced with heavier loads. At 58, avoiding
   89 |     serious injury is more valuable than marginal strength gains.
   90 |   - Hand preservation — Heavy weights build calluses and stress the hands,
   91 |     which directly affects Eric's guitar playing (acoustic flatpicking).
   92 |     The log notes callus pain on multiple occasions during heavy rows and
   93 |     shrugs. Moderate weights with more reps reduce grip-related hand stress.
   94 |   - Sustainable training — No ego lifting. Correct form at moderate weight
   95 |     over incorrect form at high weight.
   96 | 
   97 | INJURY HISTORY
   98 | 
   99 |   Prior injuries:
  100 |   - L3 disc protrusion (age 46) — Protruding lumbar disc affecting
  101 |     nerve roots serving the front thigh and knee area. Occasionally
  102 |     flares up with heavy asymmetric lifting (moving furniture, boxes).
  103 |     May have contributed to knee symptoms during heavy squats/deadlifts.
  104 |     Three years of consistent core work has built the muscular support
  105 |     that helps protect the disc. The high-rep, moderate-weight approach
  106 |     reduces compressive load on the lumbar spine per rep.
  107 |   - Lisfranc injury, left foot (~2014) — Midfoot ligament injury with
  108 |     three fractures on top of the left foot. Fully healed, usually does
  109 |     not cause problems during training. This structural history may
  110 |     contribute to subtle right-side dominance as the body compensated
  111 |     during recovery.
  112 |   - Right big toe fracture (~1996) — Partial (incomplete) fracture,
  113 |     approximately 30 years ago. Fully healed.
  114 | 
  115 |   Current/recurring:
  116 |   - Tennis elbow (lateral epicondylitis) — Chronic right bicep/forearm
  117 |     tendon injury from many years ago that never fully healed. Does not
  118 |     usually bother him currently. The high-rep, moderate-weight approach
  119 |     appears to keep it in check; heavy rows and curls were the primary
  120 |     aggravators noted in the log.
  121 |   - Right arm dominant — Right arm is stronger than left arm. Measurements
  122 |     in April 2024 confirmed asymmetry: R bicep 15.25" vs L 14.75".
  123 |     Multiple factors contribute: dominant hand preference, tennis elbow
  124 |     compensation on right side, and possible left foot Lisfranc
  125 |     compensation shifting load rightward.
  126 |   - Knee pain — Occurred at peak squat (225 lbs) and deadlift (255 lbs)
  127 |     weights in 2023. Possibly compounded by L3 disc referred pain.
  128 |     Resolved after correcting to full squat depth, reducing weight,
  129 |     and prioritizing form over load.
  130 |   - Back pain — Rarely occurs now except after heavy physical labor
  131 |     (moving furniture/boxes), which aggravates the L3 disc.
  132 |   - Wrist and shoulder pain — Occurred during heavier lifting periods;
  133 |     resolved with the shift to moderate weights and stricter form.
  134 |   - Callus/hand pain — Occasional issue with heavy grip work (rows,
  135 |     shrugs, curls); managed through the high-rep approach and necessary
  136 |     for guitar playing.
  137 |

  142 |   - Boxing (Jul-Sep 2023) — discontinued when the program ended
  143 |   - Wing Chun (Oct 2023-present) — ongoing practice; replaced qigong
  144 |   - Tai Chi (Sep 2023-2025) — periodic sessions
  145 |   - Qigong/Eight Brocades (Oct-Nov 2024) — replaced by Wing Chun
  146 |   - Yoga and Pilates (Oct 2024-Mar 2025) — added during hybrid period
  147 |   - Kickboxing (Apr 2023) — discontinued when program ended
  148 | 
  149 | Eric also trains periodically with his son Ethan, following Ethan's
  150 | programming during those sessions.
  151 | 
  152 | NUTRITION & LIFESTYLE
  153 | 
  154 | Through 2024, Eric supplemented extensively with protein powder, creatine,
  155 | and pre-workout formulas while following a high-protein diet aimed at
  156 | bulking. He discontinued supplementation after 2024. In September 2025,
  157 | he cut alcohol consumption to near-zero except for social occasions,
  158 | which correlated with a reduction in body weight and improved body
  159 | composition.

  186 | classification — at 90th percentile. A follow-up test in October 2024

  188 | superior rating, 90%).

  273 | 
  274 | NOTATION KEY
  275 | 
  276 |   WxR      Weight x Reps (e.g., 135x10 = 135 lbs for 10 reps)
  277 |   WxRxS    Weight x Reps x Sets (e.g., 95x10x10 = 95 lbs, 10 reps,
  278 |            10 sets with under 30 seconds rest between sets)
  279 |   W1xR1+W2xR2  Two set groups with 60 seconds rest between
  280 |            (e.g., 135x10+155x6 = 135 for 10, rest 60s, 155 for 6)
  281 |   (...)    Grouping for readability only, no rest implication
  282 |   60s      Explicit rest period notation
  283 |   BF/bf    Bad form (rep completed with compromised technique)
  284 |   = X,XXX  Total volume for that exercise entry (weight x total reps)
  285 | 
  286 | In the 2025-2026 data:
  287 |   x between sets = under 30 seconds rest
  288 |   + between sets = 60 seconds rest
  289 |   All rest periods in 2025 did not exceed 90 seconds
